The British Cotton Textile Industry is Brewing

To Abolish the Anglo-Japanese Commercial Treaty 49

The Boycott of Japanese Goods Movement Gradually Gains Strength

Signed a Treaty with the Netherlands to Protect Far East Territories

(London) The Executive Committee of the Cotton Industry Association today wrote to Minister of Commerce Ren Ximan about Japanese competition, saying that if Japan delays sending representatives to discuss the matter, the British government should issue a formal notice to abolish the treaty, and at the same time try to implement preferential taxes or import quotas in the markets throughout the empire to restrict imports. If the Anglo-Japanese talks reach a level where the above-mentioned measures are permissible to reconsider, then the negotiations should be revised. If the talks break down, the British government should sign a treaty with the Netherlands to protect the British and Dutch colonies in the Far East in order to resist unfair competition from the Japanese cotton industry. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(Tokyo) The Japanese officialdom is now maintaining a policy of observing the situation with a calm mind regarding the clamor in the UK. The Japanese officialdom pointed out that this clamor was initiated by the British cotton industry, with the aim of abolishing the Anglo-Japanese Commercial Treaty and making the British colonies not subject to the existing commercial treaty. The Japanese officialdom is convinced that the British government will not tolerate this clamor, because the World Economic Conference is about to open and trade talks will be held between the British and Japanese representatives. However, the Japanese business community is quite indignant that there is an anti-Japanese movement in the UK. Some business leaders advocate retaliatory plans. They acknowledge that the competition between the two countries is very fierce, but point out that British industry and commerce hold a selfish attitude and that Japan's trade with the British Empire is actually beneficial to the UK. Japan's trade with the UK has been in a state of deficit in recent years, totaling 100,000,000 Japanese yen in 1930, 96,000,000 yen in 1931, and 34,000,000 yen in 1932. Japan's trade with some British colonies has occasionally been in surplus. It has been found that these colonies are transshipment ports for Japanese goods. Japan's trade with other parts of the British Empire has always been in deficit except for last year. Last year, Japan's trade with India did gain a slight advantage, but this was a first in 27 years. It has been found that the total deficit in Japan's trade with India in these 27 years reached 3,350,000,000 yuan. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Decided to Protest Again Against the New Tax Rate

(Tokyo) The Japanese government instructed the Consul General in Nanjing on May 31 to protest against the Chinese government's implementation of the new tax rate. US President Approves

ABOLITION OF THE GOLD STANDARD ACT 70

Purpose is to extend the period of inflation

Government bonds have double protection

▲ National News, Washington, 5th. The US President signed the bill to abolish the gold standard today. This move will extend the period of inflation based on the current foundation, as the gold standard will not be restored until after Congress reconvenes at the earliest next year. During this period, the federal government will benefit the most, as it is the largest debtor, owing a total of $21,441,209,177 in public debt. In the future, it can enjoy the benefits of reduced burdens, just like farmers and homeowners who mortgage their property for loans. In addition, state and local governments across the country, which owe $100 million, will also enjoy the same benefits. According to inflation, the market price of public bonds will usually fall. However, this inflationary plan has two protections for government bonds: one is to authorize the Federal Reserve Bank to acquire 300 million yuan of government bonds, and the other is to authorize the President to issue 300 million yuan of national currency to acquire government bonds.

POLISH PRESIDENT TAKES OFFICE 71

American Round-the-World Aviator

ALREADY IN SIBERIAN FLIGHT 72

New York to Moscow in 28 and a half hours

Created a new record for non-stop flight

▲ National News, Moscow, 6th. American aviator Barton Teng rested briefly here and departed again at 1:30 AM in the moonlight, heading for Omsk in Siberia. He is expected to arrive in seven or eight hours. According to weather forecasts, there will be strong headwinds and rain along the way, with occasional heavy fog, but the weather east of Omsk should improve. Marten stayed in Moscow for less than ten hours, most of which was spent inspecting the plane. A large piece of flannel was found in an oil injector in the engine, which had fallen off the oil filter and caused an obstacle when injected into the cylinder. Marten told people that after finding this piece of flannel, it might have saved his life. Further news: Patton Teng flew over Kazan three hours after departure. His plane flew quite high, and the estimated speed was 125 miles per hour.

▲ Reuters, Moscow, 5th. American aviator Marten, who hopes to break the record for flying around the world in less than eight and a half days, arrived here at 2:05 PM today. It took him 28 hours and 45 minutes since leaving New York, exceeding the previous record of Post and Garty by three hours. When Marten flew across the Atlantic, he encountered bad weather, which prevented him from advancing according to his planned route. At 10:10 AM on Sunday morning, he made his first landing on the island of Joffrolin in southern Norway. He initially thought he had landed on the coast of Scotland, not knowing it was an island in southern Norway. The lighthouse keeper on the island reported Marten's arrival to the Norwegian capital, but the report was delayed for a long time before reaching Oslo. Since his departure, Marten had not eaten anything except oranges, so he was extremely exhausted after arriving on the island. He repaired the plane slightly, then went to bed for some time, and then flew from Joffrolin Island to the Taina military airfield, 15 miles from Oslo. After resting briefly in Oslo, he continued his journey and reached Moscow. He will now go to Irkutsk from here. Marten's plane is covered with the names of women from Joffrolin Island on both wings, as an expression of admiration for Marten's courage.

Another telegram: Marten felt very tired but very happy when he arrived here. He will sleep for a few hours and take a bath before going to Siberia. People in the Soviet aviation industry welcomed him warmly. The weather is not very good now, but Marten expects to fly at least 1,700 miles before landing. It took Marten seven hours and fifteen minutes to fly from the Taina airfield in Oslo to here. People in the Soviet aviation industry had been waiting for a long time. When Marten landed, they rushed forward to welcome him, helped him out of the plane, and put him in a Russian plane to take him into the air as a sign of respect. Marten said that he felt very good. The reason he landed in Norway was to melt the ice on the wings and to rest a little. Marten flew 4,000 miles from New York to Joffrolin Island, which is a new world record for non-stop solo flight. Marten said that he flew completely unconsciously over Ireland and England and did not see any ships when he crossed the Atlantic.

▲ Tass, Moscow, 6th. American aviator Marten, who plans to make a round-the-world flight, continued to fly to Pavlovaksk at 1:14 this morning after resting for nine hours at the Moscow airfield. He must pass through Sverdlovsk, Novosbirsk, Irkutsk and other places. The total distance from Moscow to Pavlovaksk is 6,950 kilometers.

▲ National News, Omsk, 6th. American aviator MacTeng departed from Moscow at 1:30 this morning and arrived safely here at 1:35 PM. He will rest overnight and continue tomorrow morning.

US ARMS EMBARGO ORDER 73

President Opposes Amendment

Senate Postpones Vote

▲ Havas, Washington, 5th. The bill authorizing the President to prohibit the transport of arms to belligerent countries is unlikely to be definitively put to a vote in the Senate before it convenes in January next year. Last week, the Senate Foreign Relations Committee amended the bill passed by the House of Representatives, deciding that the method of prohibiting arms exports should be applied to all belligerent countries, without making any distinction between aggressor and attacked countries. If this amendment is passed, the promises made by Roosevelt during the Washington talks and the declarations made by the US representative Davis in Geneva will lose their practical value. The establishment of this amendment is due to the resolute demands of the "isolation policy" faction. Roosevelt, upon hearing of this case, immediately declared his opposition and said that he hoped to discuss the matter again soon. However, judging from the Senate's psychology, it may not be easy to withdraw this amendment. The government seems to be aware of this, so the authorities seem to intend to delay the matter slightly, so that the Senate can change its psychology.

PUBLIC TELEGRAM 85

To the Newspaper Offices of Peiping: I, the undersigned, established this office in Zhangjiakou last year under the order of the Ministry of Military Administration, and have since supplemented several thousand horses for various troops, organs, schools, and armies. As the national crisis is increasingly urgent, we are actively purchasing and replenishing. However, Feng Yuxiang, who is entrenched in Zhangjiakou, harbors disloyal intentions and is implementing a policy of separation in the name of resisting Japan. On May 26, he used lightning-fast methods to secretly dispatch armed troops to simultaneously surround and search the Chahar Provincial Government and all its subordinate organs, arbitrarily arresting central administrative personnel. This office was particularly targeted and suffered the most. The following is a record of the whole incident. On this day, Feng sent one battalion and two companies of his 2nd Training Regiment, led by Company Commander Gan and Deputy Officer Ran, with more than 100 armed soldiers, riding to surround this office. Holding guns and live ammunition, they were more ferocious than bandits. They detained all the officers and soldiers in one room, claiming that they were acting on the order of Commander-in-Chief Feng to search this office on the pretext that it was buying horses, but was actually conducting secret work for the central government. They also said that according to the investigation, this office had 3,000 horses, 200,000 yuan in foreign currency, and dozens of guns, and interrogated each officer one by one, creating a dangerous situation and forcing them to hand over everything immediately. After repeated explanations, they were not believed. The company commander and others even checked the horse stables and forcibly took away all 94 horses and one foal that actually existed. They also demanded the key to the safe, and when they could not get it, they broke the safe with an iron hoe. They searched and took away all the cash on hand, more than 3,000 yuan, and 5,000 yuan stored in foreign currency at the Bank of Communications. They also confiscated four rifles and pistols each, and 800 rounds of ammunition. The remaining official seals, confidential telegrams, various documents, books, etc., as well as all public and private items, were all plundered. Not satisfied with this punishment, they also escorted all the officers and soldiers in the office to the battalion headquarters to demand money for horses and guns. Later, after various attempts to rescue them, they escaped safely to Peiping. Feng is a member of the National Government, and at a time when the national situation is precarious, he should be assisting the central government and working together to save the crisis. However, he is not doing this, but is colluding with bandits, occupying a territory, and privately appointing public officials, disrupting the administrative system. He claims to be resisting Japan, but he does not rise up at a time of war emergency. He uses the false name of recruiting soldiers, but implements it at a time when military affairs have just been settled. His conspiracy to cause chaos is now evident. I, Peng, have suffered this unexpected disaster and suffered great losses. I am especially afraid that before the violent Japanese are eliminated, civil war will break out first. Therefore, I am specially reporting the circumstances of his abnormal actions and the situation of this office's plight, hoping that you will investigate it. Bai Yupeng, Director of the Zhangjiakou Military Horse Replenishment Office of the Ministry of Military Administration, respectfully presents this report.

Japanese and Puppet Troops Begin Activities in Eastern Chahar · Reaches 86

The Japanese Cavalry in Dolon has been Ordered to Guard Against the Puppet Army's Advance Southward

Feng is Consolidating his Army and Preparing for War in Zhangjiakou, with Meetings Held Daily in Pingfang

A Special Dispatch from Beiping: After the signing of the armistice agreement by the Japanese, they shifted their focus to Chahar Province and paid close attention to Feng's assumption of the position of Commander-in-Chief of the Anti-Japanese Allied Army. On the 2nd of this month, they ordered the Motegi Cavalry in Dolon to pay special attention to the traitor Liu Guitang's forces. It was already on the 31st that they invaded Guyuan from Dolon. The traitorous troops of Cui Xinwu and others have also begun to stir, and the situation in eastern Chahar is gradually becoming tense. Since taking office, Feng has spared no effort in consolidating his army and preparing for war. On one hand, he has expanded his guard, and on the other hand, he has incorporated miscellaneous troops and militia. Near Zhangjiakou, there are about 10,000 troops expanded from Feng's guard, as well as several thousand troops from Li Fuying's Jin army. In the Zhangbei area, in addition to the original garrison of Zhao Chengzhou's Jin army cavalry division, Zhang Lisheng's cavalry commander, also has arrived. Feng Zhanhai's volunteer army was reorganized by Feng into the Anti-Japanese Army, and Feng Zhanhai was appointed as the commander-in-chief, leading his troops to be stationed in the Baochang area. Feng's troops are stationed all the way from Zhangjiakou to Xuanhua. Fang Zhenwu's troops are stationed in Xuanhua, Dushikou, and other places, while Sun Dianying's troops are stationed in the area of ​​Chicheng, Yanqing, and Shacheng. According to current statistics, the various troops and militia in Chahar number no less than 200,000. If the Japanese army does invade Chahar, they will be sufficient to resist. However, the system is complex, and both supplies and equipment are lacking. It is difficult to say whether they can cope with a strong enemy. Pingfang has been convening military meetings for days to discuss and resolve the issues of puppet troops in the war zone and the transfer of our troops after the withdrawal of the Japanese army. The matter of Chahar is also being discussed in detail. The attitude toward Feng's actions has yet to be stated; however, tight defenses are being maintained around Juyongguan to prevent accidents. Today, a certain military organization in Pingfang received a telegram from Zhao Chengzhou reporting on the Chahar situation and requesting a transfer. The telegram stated that Feng (Yuxiang) has appointed cavalry division commanders Nie Yuling, Zhang Ziguang, Cao Fuchen, and army commander Zhang Lisheng, and 24th Division commander Fu Chun, and they are all now in Zhangbei, incorporating bandits and recruiting old troops. The number of troops near Zhangbei has reached several thousand, and they are living mixed in with my troops. If anything happens, combat will definitely be inconvenient. I intend to move my troops to the area west of Zhangbei. If the Japanese and puppet troops change course and invade southward, I will lead my troops to threaten the enemy's flanks and can easily coordinate with my Li (Fuying) army. Furthermore, according to people from Zhangjiakou, Feng Yuxiang is loudly advocating thorough resistance against Japan. He has been living in seclusion in Zhangjiakou, harboring the idea of ​​returning to the battlefield to try his hand again. He has been secretly making arrangements for more than a day, and there are many people contacting him from all sides. In late last month, Fang Zhenwu led his Zhang (Renjie) and Bao (Gang) armies, claiming to number 40,000 to 50,000, and marched directly into Xuanhua, disarming a large portion of He Sui's newly compiled 55th Army. The internal atmosphere in Chahar suddenly became very tense. At the same time, Feng Zhanhai led tens of thousands of volunteer soldiers to Zhangbei. The advance troops had already entered Zhangjiakou, demanding supplies along the way, causing panic among the people. Wealthy households moved to Wanquan one after another. At that time, the voice of "Sino-Japanese Compromise" was singing loudly, and Feng suddenly rose up and detained Feng Zhanhai, sending 2,000 of his guards to disarm all the volunteer soldiers throughout the night of the 25th of last month. That night, the sound of mobilization slogans filled the streets, startling the citizens and causing them to think that a great disaster was about to befall them. It is expected that other problems will not occur in the shortest period of time. As for the Ping-Sui Railway line, Feng's army has placed a platoon of infantry at Kangzhuang Station, specializing in inspecting passengers and goods on trains. The inspection of plainclothes passengers is very lenient, but it is very strict for soldiers. If armed soldiers do not have badges, they are detained according to Feng's orders. Zhang Zuolin's Will 89

(Six Years in an Instant Since the Huanggutun Incident)

What Does Zhang Xueliang Think in a Foreign Country?

A Special Dispatch from Beiping: June 4 is the tragic anniversary of the assassination of Grand Marshal Zhang Zuolin by the enemy in Huanggutun. His son, Xueliang, is now far away in a foreign country. What does he think about it? Previously, after Zhang Zuolin's military defeat, he telegraphed his resignation on June 2 of the 16th year of the Republic and left Beijing for Fengtian on the 3rd. The security of Beijing was handed over to the Temporary Security Maintenance Committee composed of Wang Shizhen, Xiong Xiling, and others. On the 4th, Zhang's special train arrived at the intersection of the Beijing-Fengtian and South Manchurian Railways on the South Manchurian Railway. Suddenly, a bomb exploded, and the special train was blown to pieces. Zhang was seriously injured and died in Shenyang on the 9th. Wu Junsheng, the Governor of Heilongjiang, was also killed in the bombing. Wu was succeeded by Wan Fulin as the Governor of Heilongjiang, and Zhang Xueliang concurrently served as the Commander of the Northeast Border Defense. When the September 18th Incident occurred, Zhang Xueliang stated that he would definitely avenge the national and family hatred. Although he is now traveling overseas, it is thought that he must not forget the painful memories of that day. Before Zhang Zuolin was killed, he had a will, which spoke of promoting unification. The original text is rarely known to outsiders. Now, through a certain important person in the Northeast, the reporter has obtained the original text, which is recorded as follows:

"I am unfortunately in danger on the way back, and my illness is now serious. I am afraid I will die soon. Since I joined the army as a child, I have sworn to serve the country with my life and put life and death aside. I am now fifty-four years old, and death is not ordained by heaven, but I cannot help but feel uneasy because my ambition to save the country has not been fulfilled. Now I entrust the important task of Fengtian to Xueliang, hoping that you will manage it well, recruit talented people, improve internal affairs, make the people live and work in peace, and comfort the longings of the elders. On the one hand, strive for peace to end the war and promote unification, do not go against my previous telegrams advocating peace, and I hope that my comrades will share this idea and follow my will, giving priority to the country and the people in everything, and working together. This will be enough to show the sincerity of love among all of you. Even if I die, I will rest in peace." (Jin)

Wuxi 90

The First Installment of Land Value Tax Collection Begins

After the amalgamation of the local Finance Bureau and the County, the collection of silver tax is handled by the second section of the county government, supervised by the Land Tax Director, Zhu Kaiguan. In order to strictly pursue arrears, County Magistrate Yan convened more than 400 village heads from the entire county twice, speaking earnestly about the first installment of land value tax for this year, deciding to start collection on July 1. The Land Tax Office instructed the clerks in the Yi and Gui districts to rush to prepare the registration booklets overnight. The booklet paper was printed and distributed by the county government. As soon as all the booklets are completed, they must be sent to the county for stamping. In recent days, farmers from the four villages have been coming to the city to pay land value tax to the county and collect licenses, which is very enthusiastic. At the same time, the Land Tax Office also instructed the collection officials in the seventeen cities and villages to go to the villages to strictly urge the large clans and wealthy households to quickly pay up to support the national treasury.

Jiangzhen 91

Cultivating the Unclaimed Coastal Land North of the Yangtze River

Last autumn, officials and merchants discussed jointly cultivating the barren coastal salt lands north of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu Province. A plan was drawn up, with a total cost of 10 million yuan, with officials and merchants each contributing 5 million. In April of this year, they began to proceed separately. Initially, it was proposed that the merchants would raise 25 million first, and the officials would allocate funds from the Finance Department. According to reliable information, the 5 million that the merchants should be responsible for has been negotiated with Rong Zongjing, and all the loans will be paid in three installments by the end of this year. The loan agreement will be signed in mid-month, so the funding can be temporarily resolved. As for the official 5 million, Finance Director Shu Shifu has also assured people that he is making every effort to raise funds. Currently, the first part of the project in the reclamation zone is to improve the soil quality and flush the saline-alkali land. Starting on the 1st of this month, 30,000 workers will be hired to excavate a new canal. This canal starts from Chenjiagang in Lianshui and ends at Jiaozhen in Nantong, so as to draw water from the Huai River into the canal, divert the flow for flushing, and it is limited to be completed within this year. In addition, 500 soil-turning machines have been ordered from Germany for digging up the sandy soil in the area. A batch has now been shipped.

Hangzhou 92

The Situation After the Commencement of Land Value Tax Collection

Hangzhou's land value tax has been in preparation for more than a year and officially began to be collected on the 1st of this month. The Municipal Finance Section has set up a collection office to implement the collection. According to the land value tax regulations, the first half of this month is the bonus period, and the citizens have a deep understanding of this new tax. Therefore, in recent days, many people have gone to collect land value licenses and pay taxes, especially large households. In total, about 300 households have submitted payments in five or six days, and the tax payments amount to more than 1,000 yuan, which shows the enthusiasm.

Xiaoshan 93

Fishermen Strive for Baima Lake

Since Dong Xiaohou, a gentleman from the southern township of Xiaoshan, rented Baima Lake from Zhejiang University to raise fish, thousands of nearby fishing households have repeatedly petitioned the provincial and county governments to cancel the lease and help thousands of fishermen who have lost their livelihoods. Unexpectedly, the provincial committee's visit to Xiaoshan still did not produce satisfactory results. More than 8,000 fishing households have now petitioned the Central Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, with a strong determination to continue until their goals are achieved.

Heavy Rain Sinks Boat, Drowning Two Children

At noon on the 4th, the weather suddenly changed, and heavy rain poured down. The streets and alleys were flooded with water several feet deep. A fast boat belonging to Xiao Yangfan from the eastern township, traveling from Shao to Kai and Su, sank due to the heavy rain, strong winds, and overweight boat. Fortunately, there were fishing boats nearby that tried their best to rescue them. All 27 passengers were rescued except for two children who are still missing. The foreign goods and cargo they brought, worth about two or three hundred yuan, all fell into the river.

Ma Zhanshan, the national hero and Chairman of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, and Su Bingwen, the Commander-in-Chief of the National Salvation Army, arrived in Shanghai by Italian mail ship at 10 p.m. the night before last and stayed at the Army Club on Jinxian Road, where they were warmly welcomed by various groups and the public. At 3 p.m., Generals Ma and Su jointly boarded a train at the Zhenru Railway Station to go to Beijing to report to the Central Government on the anti-Japanese and anti-Russian experiences and advise on major plans for resisting Japan. Generals Ma and Su, in view of the enthusiastic assistance from all sectors in Shanghai to the anti-Japanese cause in the past, and the enthusiastic welcome from all sectors when the Conte Rosso arrived at the port the night before last, visited leaders from all sectors together in the same car at 9 a.m. yesterday to thank them for their warm welcome and hospitality. The two first went to visit Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Yang Xiaotian, Director of the City Security Department, and then visited General Zhu Ziqiao, representing the Volunteer Army, and Chu Huiseng, representing the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association. Receiving Reporters 97

At 11 a.m. yesterday, Generals Ma and Su received reporters from various newspapers at the Army Club on Jinxian Road, with more than 20 people present. At that time, the Lianhua Company also filmed a movie. After Ma said a few words of greeting, he first expressed his gratitude and apologized for not having time to talk in detail on the ship.

Anti-Japanese is a Friend 98

The reporter asked, "How many of Chairman Ma's old troops are still there and where are they currently stationed?" (Ma replied) "About 20,000, currently stationed in Chahar Province." (Asked) "Commander Deng of your troops is cooperating with Feng Huanzhang in resisting Japan. What are Chairman's opinions?" (Answered) "I have not received a telegram and do not know the details. However, resisting Japan is my long-cherished wish, and all those who can truly resist Japan are my friends and can cooperate." (Asked) "Feng Yuxiang's actions in Chahar seem to be inconsistent with the central government's political views. What is your opinion?" (Answered) "I have been away from the country for half a year, and the situation is not clear. I don't know the details." (Asked) "After Chairman goes to Beijing, do you intend to go to Chahar?" (Answered) "I intend to go to Chahar to inspect my old troops and implement the anti-Japanese proposition."

Thoughts on the Ceasefire 99

(Asked) "What are Chairman's thoughts on the signing of the North China Armistice Agreement?" (Answered) "When the North China Armistice Agreement was signed, I was on my way back to the country and did not know the content, so it is not convenient to express my opinion. My personal opinion is that for the sake of rectifying the military appearance, a temporary local ceasefire is not impossible. The public should also understand the government's difficulties, but it is absolutely impossible to compromise and surrender." (Asked) "When you return to the country and go to Beijing, will you make any contributions to the central government?" (Answered) "We have been fighting against Japan for years and know more about the situation of the Japanese army. Of course, we will report to the central government and advise on everything. As for the future policy, it will be determined according to the central government's policy. However, the people of the whole country are like this, and the central government will never compromise with Japan." At this point, General Su Bingwen spoke, saying that the ceasefire was definitely not the government's intention, but a temporary measure to cope with the situation. Compromising with Japan would violate the public opinion of the whole country. Even with our stupidity, we would not do this. How could the central leaders be so confused?

Impressions of Russia and Germany 100

(Reporter asked) "What are General Ma's impressions of the Soviet Union's hospitality during this trip?" (Answered) "The Soviet Union treated us entirely as a neutral country. During our stay in the country, all our comings and goings were monitored everywhere, but in fact we were never subjected to any abuse." (Asked) "After traveling to the Soviet Union, General Ma also went to Germany. The political systems of these two countries are extremely opposite. What is the general's comparative observation?" (Answered) "Although the Soviet Union is nominally a socialist country, in reality, it still takes into account its national position everywhere. For example, foreign goods cannot be sold in its country at all. Its citizens would rather wear burlap sacks than spend money to buy foreign goods. As for Germany, although the domestic political situation is also very complicated, everything is still based on the country as the premise. Recently, Hitler's assumption of power has shown the new spirit of the nation everywhere. Meetings and parades are all lively. The most admirable thing is the German people's affection for the army, which is not like the fear of soldiers among our people. This is what we soldiers are extremely ashamed of."

[丨>Generals Ma and Su Receive Reporters (Li Zunyong and Xu Tianzhang Together)<丨]

Meeting Zhang in Italy 101

(Reporter asked) "When General Ma met with Mr. Zhang Hanqing in Italy, did he talk about national affairs?" (Answered) "Mr. Zhang only told me that he was ill and was currently recuperating. He did not express anything about national affairs." Ma also said that when we were in Europe, people from various countries paid attention to our words and deeds, and expressed sympathy for our firm anti-Japanese proposition. When we passed through Hong Kong, we were deeply grateful for the enthusiastic welcome from representatives of various sectors and groups on the ship. Liu Luyin, representing the Southwest Political Committee, did not meet on the ship. Mr. Hu Qingtang sent his daughter, Mulan, to talk and invited us to go ashore to meet, but I also declined due to illness.

Future Propositions 102

Are you prepared to make any announcements?" (General Su answered) "We Chinese soldiers only know how to obey government orders and are not convenient to make any propositions. Moreover, we have been away from the country for half a year, and all the changes are not known in detail." General Ma remained silent in his seat, politely telling the reporter that many situations were unclear during his time abroad, so it was difficult to express his opinion.

Going to Jiangxi is Undecided 103

In addition, there is still a brigade that followed Chairman Ma's troops to garrison in Chahar, and has now been reorganized into a training regiment." (Asked) "Will General Su go to Xinjiang?" (Answered) "I have no intention of doing so." (Asked) "Will Generals Ma and Su go to Jiangxi to visit Chairman Chiang?" (Answered) "It will be decided after going to Beijing."

Levying Anti-Dumping Duties

To Be Handled by Customs 109

Tax Rate Based on Market Conditions

The Ministry of Finance, considering that the dumping of foreign goods affects the development of Chinese industries, intends to levy anti-dumping duties on foreign goods to protect domestic products and balance the prices of foreign goods. It will also establish an anti-dumping committee to conduct detailed investigations into all dumped goods to provide a basis for levying duties. It is learned that since the committee's investigation, the various dumped goods have been generally clarified. This time, the anti-dumping duty is levied to balance prices, so the tax must determine a tax rate, and is based on market conditions as the standard. If a certain product costs ten yuan for domestic goods, but only six yuan for foreign goods, a dumping tax of four yuan will be levied in the future. If the foreign goods are not available domestically and are being dumped among foreign merchants, then no additional dumping tax will be added. It is also heard that, for the sake of convenience, the collection of this tax will be entrusted to the Customs in the future, but the principles of collection will be determined by the review committee and notified to the Customs at any time. The actual implementation date has not yet been determined.

Industrial Circles Approve

Loan to Purchase American Cotton and Wheat 110

Says it will not affect our agricultural products

According to the Huadong News Agency, Finance Minister Song Ziwen signed a loan of 50 million US dollars in the United States, of which four-fifths will be used to purchase American cotton and one-fifth to purchase American wheat. This matter is of great importance to our economy and industry. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency specially visited yarn and flour mill manufacturers yesterday to inquire about their opinions. The results obtained were all in agreement. The interview is recorded as follows:

The Yarn Industry stated that, according to Hu Yunjie, director of the Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange, China's cotton production could be self-sufficient, but due to years of being bought up by the Japanese, raw materials have become increasingly scarce. Japanese yarn is being dumped on the market, while Chinese yarn is greatly affected due to the high cost of raw materials and the low price of yarn. In this difficult period, there is even more panic. Before leaving the country, Mr. Song had fully considered this matter, and the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry also made a decision to purchase American cotton on credit at the meeting to help yarn mills in Shanghai. This shows that the arrival of American cotton in China will not have much impact. However, the current price of American cotton is about 60 yuan in Chinese currency, while Chinese cotton is only about 46 yuan. Therefore, after shipping to China, it is hoped that the Ministry of Finance can sell it at 80% of the price, so that Chinese merchants can enthusiastically purchase it. Regarding the payment method, it would be especially desirable if payments could be made in installments. The government purchases this raw material on credit, and the debt must be cleared after three years, while merchants pay at most in two or three months. The government can immediately obtain a large sum of money, which is more cost-effective than issuing public bonds, even though the selling price has been discounted by 20%. Moreover, it can increase customs revenue. The yarn mills will convene a meeting in the near future to decide which companies will purchase the cotton. The import of American cotton will inevitably affect domestic products, but the maximum monthly import is only about 50,000 bales, so it will not have much impact.

The Flour Industry stated that, according to Rong Zongjing's associates, the production of wheat flour in China has been very low recently. Since the loss of the Northeast, raw materials have become even more scarce. The national production is only enough for the needs of two or three days for a few manufacturers. Therefore, flour mill manufacturers have to continuously purchase foreign wheat from the United States, Australia, and other places to maintain business and take care of the lives of workers. Therefore, Finance Minister Song's decision to purchase American wheat on credit will absolutely not have any impact on our country.

Japanese Ambassador Going to Capital This Morning 111

To Protest Our New Tax Rates

Datong News Agency reports that regarding the issue of Japanese merchants opposing our implementation of new tax rates, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an emergency instruction to Shanghai yesterday, ordering Japanese Ambassador to China, Akira Ariyoshi, to immediately lodge a protest with us and request that we redraft the tax rates. It is learned that Ariyoshi has decided to go to the capital this morning to handle this matter. The details are recorded as follows:

(Japanese Ambassador Received Instructions)

After our country implemented new tax rates, the United Federation of Japanese Commercial Associations in this port convened a meeting of all Japanese merchant representatives in Shanghai at the Wengjianshi Road Club to discuss countermeasures. It was unanimously decided to send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Japan to lodge a protest with us. After receiving the telegram, the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs immediately telegraphed the Consul-General stationed in Beijing to thoroughly investigate the new tax rates implemented by our country in order to prepare for the protest. It is learned that the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an emergency instruction to Shanghai yesterday, ordering Japanese Ambassador to China, Akira Ariyoshi, to immediately lodge a verbal protest with our diplomatic authorities. At around 3:00 PM yesterday, Ariyoshi telegraphed to invite Consul Ishisa of the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai and representatives of various Japanese factories to a meeting to discuss the reasons for the protest. Hengzhu, the Japanese Commercial Counselor in China, did not return to Shanghai yet, so he specially sent a representative to attend the meeting. Because the Japanese side is strictly guarding secrets, it is difficult to find out the results.

(Decision to Go to Capital This Morning)

According to sources from the Japanese Consul-General, Ambassador Ariyoshi, together with his secretary and Chinese translator, etc., eight people in total, is scheduled to take the Beijing-Shanghai Express train at 9:25 this morning to go to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to discuss certain diplomatic matters. However, it is still difficult to determine whether it is related to the issue of opposing the implementation of new tax rates. However, according to Japanese merchants, Ariyoshi's mission this time is to protest the implementation of these new tax rates to our diplomatic authorities. The minimum goal must be to achieve a revision. If the verbal protest is ineffective, the Japanese government will order the expulsion of all Chinese overseas in Japan as retaliation. The second step is to actively establish Japanese goods manufacturing factories in Shanghai to reduce the import tax payable on Japanese goods.

Page 10

Female Aviator Lin Pengxia

Thoughts on Returning from the Northwest 112

To Reclaim the Northeast

Northwest Must Be Developed

Ms. Lin Pengxia, China's first female aviator, was warmly welcomed when she inspected various provinces in Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Ningxia, Suiyuan, and Chahar. She returned to Shanghai from Tianjin the day before yesterday. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specially visited her at her hotel to inquire about her experience and thoughts on the inspection of the Northwest. She agreed to meet, her face was quite thin, but she spoke eloquently. She said that her ancestral home is Putian, and after graduating from Shanghai Minli Girls' High School and Tianjin Girls' High School, she followed her father to Nanyang to do business, and then studied at Columbia University in the United States, where she obtained a Bachelor of Economics degree. She also went to England to study aviation piloting and served as the manager of a rubber plantation in Singapore. After the September 18th Incident and the loss of the Northeast, and seeing Japanese planes flying and bombing, and compatriots suffering, she felt that the Northwest must be developed urgently. Therefore, with a spirit of fearlessness, she went to the Northwest. She saw that the provinces had vast land and sparse population, with an average of less than a few people per mile, and the richness of the resources was far beyond our expectations. Taking coal as an example, it is everywhere. Metal and other minerals are also found everywhere, but unfortunately, they have not been mined. Culture is blocked due to traffic congestion. The locals regard my solo travels as a strange thing. The customs are honest and sincere. Smokers account for an average of 70-80%. The Shaanxi-Gansu area has suffered from drought for years, commerce is sluggish, and the economy is depressed. People mainly eat wheat flour. The disaster areas are vast and numerous. Last month, there was another wind disaster, and the wheat harvest is completely hopeless. The only relief at present is replanting. Chairman Shao's planning for remedies is extremely needed. The weak among the disaster-stricken people are reduced to ditches, and the strong become bandits. It is difficult to suppress or appease them. In short, I feel that if China wants to reclaim the Northeast, it should develop the Northwest. If it wants to develop the Northwest, it should help the Northwest, starting with investigations. This time, when I came to Shanghai, I planned to ask academic and economic groups to speed up their work, and seek sincere comrades to gather and study, and be the pioneers of actual development. The Ningxia Education Department sent me off when I returned south. It is said that yesterday, Ms. Lin also gave a lecture on developing the border and promoting culture at the invitation of Wuben Girls' High School and the Frontier Research Association of Shanghai University, which greatly moved the teachers and students. She was praised as a remarkable woman in China.

Departing for Philippines Today, Will Still Come to Shanghai

Sun Ke and Chen Gongbo Going to Capital 116

Sun Ke and Chen Gongbo Took Night Train to the Capital Last Night

Feng Yuxiang Aims to Resist Japan

Japanese Rumors Are Increasingly Bizarre

Yesterday, a reporter visited someone in Shanghai close to Feng Yuxiang to inquire about Feng's situation. According to him, Feng organized the People's Anti-Japanese Allied Army. The Japanese side is eager to eliminate and destroy it, but due to the facts, it is impossible to introduce it to the world. The actions of Feng reported in the newspapers recently, the most laughable is the report of a Japanese news agency that Feng has severed ties with the Kuomintang, banned the Qingbai flag, and plans to restore relations with Soviet Russia. It is purely fabricated, trying to incite civil war, which is absolutely inconsistent with the facts. We appeal to common sense, ask whether Feng has the need to sever ties with the Kuomintang or the possibility of allying with Russia. Other rumors are lengthy, and I don't want to justify them any further. It is best to ask the press to organize a reporter group to go to Zhangjiakou to conduct an on-the-spot investigation to know the truth. Feng aims to resist Japan, and his situation is tragic. The Japanese army will inevitably invade Chahar. When the time comes to bravely resist foreign aggression, the facts will prove it.

Jiangsu Construction Director Dong Xiujia Came to Shanghai to Raise Funds for Road Construction 117

Guo Xishi Attended the Joint Committee on Sericulture in Jiangsu and Zhejiang

Came to Shanghai to Borrow Funds for Road Construction

According to a "Shen Shi Telegraph News Agency" report from this port, Dong Xiujia, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, came to Shanghai to contact the banking community to borrow funds because the funds for the construction of Jiangsu roads are insufficient. Guo Xishi participated in the Joint Committee on Sericulture in Jiangsu and Zhejiang and visited the Provincial Agricultural Farm and Agricultural Implement Manufacturing Plant. He came to Shanghai on the 5th. A reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency specially visited him at his hotel and was received and gave the following interview:

Raising Funds for Road Construction, according to Dong, the most important thing for construction right now is to build roads. Convenient transportation can stabilize prices and avoid the risk of famine. However, due to the shortage of provincial treasury funds, it is necessary to contact the banking community in Shanghai to borrow funds so that the planned highways can be built section by section. He has already contacted the banking community several times with Shu Shifu, Director of the Finance Department, and there is good hope of success.

Attending the Joint Committee, Dong continued, while in Wuxi, he attended the meeting convened by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Sericulture Control Committee to restrict cocoon prices in Jiangsu. Because the weather in Jiangsu Province this year is excellent, the sericulture harvest is more than 80-90%. However, there are very few silkworm farmers. Judging from the current market, there is a shortage of supply. The Control Committee is afraid that the cocoon industry will arbitrarily release prices, which will affect the silk market. If silk prices are too high, it is not easy to export. For example, last year's old silk was rescued by the government for more than 3 million yuan before it could be exported. It is better to restrict cocoon prices in advance than to plan for relief in the future. Therefore, the final decision is that the improved seeds should not exceed 40 yuan per dan. If cocoon companies exceed this price, the government will revoke their licenses. The Wuxi cocoon merchants are quite able to comply. Therefore, the silk market this year will definitely not be as stagnant as last year.

Visiting the Agricultural Farm, Dong continued, after attending the restriction meeting, he visited the Provincial Agricultural Experiment Farm and the Sericulture Control Office. The instruments and equipment used are quite complete, and the work is also very diligent. In the future, inferior mulberry and inferior seeds will be completely banned. Finally, he visited the Agricultural Implement Manufacturing Plant. The water pumps and engines recently produced by the plant after a long period of research and improvement are quite comparable to imported products, which is a good phenomenon for my country's agriculture.

Plan for Water and Electricity Facilities in the City Center Area Has Been Determined 120

Water Supply Facilities Are Being Implemented Sequentially

Electrical Engineering to Be Completed This Year

The City Government's new building and the temporary buildings of various bureaus in the city center area are being actively constructed and will soon be completed. The plan for all water and electrical equipment in the area, drawn up by the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company at the order of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, has been discussed and agreed upon by all parties concerned and submitted to the Mayor for approval. The Mayor has approved it at the 237th Municipal Affairs Conference and will implement it immediately. The agreed-upon measures are recorded as follows:

Water Supply Problem The measures that have been decided on the water supply aspect are roughly: (A) Zhabei will lay water pipes to all the most needed areas, and the rest will be laid sequentially at any time; (B) the cost of the first phase of pipe laying is estimated at 160,000 yuan; (C) the City Government guarantees that the annual water and electricity fees will be sufficient to cover 12% of the actual construction cost of the main pipe within five years. If there is a shortfall, the City Government will make it up. The cost of branch pipes other than the main pipe will be borne by the users.

Electrical Problem The measures discussed on the electrical problem are as follows: (A) Two underground cables will be used to connect the main transformer station on Xiangyin Road directly to both sides of the park, and then overhead lines will be used to form a ring, and then underground cables will be used to connect the twelve open-air booths; (B) low-voltage connection will be used for each area where the open-air booths are powered. If one open-air booth is damaged, it can be divided into two parts and powered by the nearby open-air booths to reduce the power transmission time. The above construction will be determined in order of priority according to the urgency of needs, but must be completed by the end of 1933; (C) The method of the City Government guaranteeing electricity revenue, excluding street lights, is the same as that for water supply.

County-Level Agencies

Petition to Postpone the Establishment of a Water Patrol Team 123

The county-level agencies under the Shanghai County government submitted a document to the Civil Affairs Department, the Provincial Government, and the County Government, requesting postponement of the establishment of a water patrol team due to insufficient financial resources. The document stated: "Regarding the establishment of a water patrol team in this county, it was previously resolved by the council convened by your government that the joint meetings of various districts should discuss and decide on fundraising and management methods and report to the county, and then convene another meeting to make a decision, etc. After detailed discussion by Shi Jie and others, it was unanimously agreed that the chief magistrate's concern for the people's welfare and attention to waterborne security is indeed an act of benefiting the locality and should be followed. However, since the division of the city and county in this county, the essence of the city has all gone to the municipal government, and the remaining six districts are all impoverished rural areas with a population of less than 120,000 and an area of less than 500 li. Although the waterways in this county are numerous, the land area is not vast. Furthermore, in addition to the Huangpu River, the remaining waterways in this county are small and scattered ports with inconvenient passage for ships. Moreover, the First District Department of the Provincial Public Security Water Police is stationed here, and tax police patrol boats patrol from time to time, which is sufficient to maintain security. In addition, in recent years, all industries have been depressed, and taxes have been heavy. Starting last year, an additional fee for Qing Dynasty documents of one jiao per mu was levied, which has exceeded 2% of the land price. Even other donations and taxes have been exhausted, making it inconvenient to increase further. Therefore, although the public has the desire to increase police force and maintain security, they deeply feel powerless to contribute due to economic exhaustion. After repeated consideration, Shi Jie and others unanimously believe that this matter can be postponed. We hereby submit a joint petition to your esteemed chief magistrate, reporting the actual situation of the above-mentioned locality and the difficulties in fundraising, requesting that you, with your understanding, allow the temporary postponement of the establishment of the water patrol team in this county. Once the people's strength is slightly restored and funds are available, we will then organize the team in accordance with the regulations. If there is anything inappropriate, we respectfully request your review and approval, which would be in the public interest. Respectfully submitted by Jiang Shijie, Director of the Shanghai County Public Funds and Public Property Management Office; Wang Yiren, Chief of the Sixth District; Wu Shifang, Chief of the First District; Huang Xingrang, Director of the County Farmers' Association; Peng Zhaotang, Chief of the Second District; Zhang Yi, Director of the County Education Association; Sun Shiben, Chief of the Third District; Zhang Jingling, Chairman of the Minhang Chamber of Commerce; Fu Dianying, Chief of the Fourth District; Zhang Yunxuan, Chairman of the Sanlin Chamber of Commerce; Xing Zhigang, Chief of the Fifth District; and Tu Bingjun, Chairman of the Maqiao Chamber of Commerce."

Wu Song Vehicle and Boat Taxes Cannot Be Reduced 126

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously submitted a request to the Municipal Government to order the relevant bureaus to reduce or exempt the small vehicle and small boat taxes in Wu Song to facilitate the economic recovery of Wu Song. It is learned that the Municipal Government replied to the Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "Your submission has been noted. After consulting with the Public Utilities and Finance Bureaus, it was reported that the Wu Song small vehicle tax has been approved by your government to be reduced for six months starting from April of this year. The reduction period has just begun, and it is too early to assess the actual benefits of the tax reduction for small vehicles. The request for extension seems unnecessary. Regarding the request to exempt Wu Song sampans from registration and tax payment, the situation has been previously reported, making it difficult to make changes. According to the Public Utilities Bureau's investigation, the Wu Song sampans that are currently registered are engaged in lighterage operations in the city and are not struggling. Furthermore, the license fees paid at the time of registration can be refunded when the license is returned in accordance with the regulations, so the boat owners do not actually suffer any losses. The Finance Bureau's investigation shows that these boats are taxed at the lowest rate of 50 cents per month, which is a very small amount and cannot be reduced. Our bureaus have also reviewed that the boat owners' representatives, Gu Chuanlang and others, previously requested a 50% reduction in taxes and asked various shops to request tax exemption on their behalf, which seems contradictory and not from the boat owners' original intention, and should be rejected. In addition to instructions, this reply is hereby issued. Please inform them accordingly."

Zhejiang Waters Pirates Gradually Eliminated 127

Ouyang Ge's Letter to the Ningbo Association Reports

Patrols by Yongping and Other Warships are Sent During the Fishing Season

The Ningbo Association in Shanghai received a letter yesterday from Ouyang Ge, the commander of the Second Brigade of the Zhejiang Water Police, reporting on the progress of work and the suppression of bandits. The details are quite thorough, so excerpts are recorded below:

"Regarding the work situation, the unrest in the Zhejiang waters in recent years is undeniable. However, the lack of training for the water police, the absence of motors on patrol boats, the lack of repairs to warships, and the incompleteness of weapons all hinder the progress of arrest operations. We had planned to actively reorganize, but due to financial constraints, we were unable to fully implement our plans. We have only focused on reorganization within the possible scope, training the water police and closely instructing subordinates. In recent months, although we have not been able to achieve everything perfectly, we have cracked more than twenty major robbery cases, arrested more than sixty bandits, and rescued a total of more than one hundred hostages.

Regarding the bandit suppression process, in the battle of Baiyan, Wenling, the notorious bandits Zhang Zhuqing and Ying Zhaocai, as well as more than ten other bandits, were killed. In the battle of Chongfu, Linhai, more than two thousand tins of kerosene from the Guanghua Company and four shipmates were intercepted. After the Yongchuan merchant ship was robbed, a number of criminals who were hiding stolen goods, including Xu Rende, were detected in Dachen Mountain, along with many stolen items. Recently, in Xiaoyao Gate, Dinghai, there was a long and fierce battle with the bandits, killing several, capturing two alive, seizing three pirate ships, and rescuing twenty-three refugees, as well as many stolen items such as matches and kerosene. Also, twenty-two refugees and six large and small sailing boats were rescued in Dongji Mountain. When the Ning aluminum company's Nanxing ship recently ran aground on the grinding disc in Haimen and encountered bandits, the Yongping and other ships, as well as the fourth platoon, were ordered to rush to rescue. Unfortunately, the ships were sailing vessels and could not arrive instantly, so the rescue was not perfect. All the escaped bandits are still being actively investigated.

To protect fishermen and merchants, during the current fishing season, the Yongping, Taian, and Xinbinshun ships, as well as special forces, have been dispatched to the fishing areas to patrol and suppress bandits, with Inspector Xu as the commander-in-chief, temporarily stationed in Haimen to supervise operations. Now that the major bandit gangs have been gradually annihilated, they have become less visible. The small, scattered bandits who harass fishermen and merchants are moving around in various locations, making it exhausting to pursue them. Patrol ships are cruising along the coast at all times, and patrol boats are also deployed in various locations, never slacking. We are doing our best, but we dare not claim complete success."

French Concession Police

Trial Opens in the Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Case 128

(Yin Jiafu Was a Soldier in the 19th Route Army)

Police Detectives Search Wu Mai's Residence

The Arguments in the Case Conclude, and the Verdict Will Be Announced on a Scheduled Date

Following the successive bombings of various foreign goods stores, such as Ri Xin Zeng, De Sheng Xiang, De Feng Xiang, Fu Xiang Ji, and Lü Tai Chang, as well as other foreign goods and cotton stores, along French Avenue, by the Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group, which involved throwing bombs, damaging doors, windows, glass, and goods, and occasionally injuring store employees, the French Concession Police paid close attention to the matter as a disruption to order and security. Detectives, both Chinese and foreign, were instructed to strictly investigate the case. However, the whereabouts of these individuals were extremely secret, making it difficult to crack the case. Until noon on the 3rd of this month, Detective No. 323 of the Political Department of the French Concession Police received a tip that a secret meeting was being held on the third floor of the Wei Zhen Guangdong Food Store at No. 45 Kai Zi Er Road at 6:00 PM to discuss illegal activities. The detective reported this to Deputy Police Commissioner and Department Chief Rao Boze (transliteration), who ordered Ma Muya (transliteration), the director of the investigation department, to lead Chinese and foreign detectives to rush to the location at the specified time (No. 45 Kai Zi Er Road, i.e., Daode Lane). They saw two people going upstairs, and the detectives rushed to the third floor to arrest them. However, one person had already escaped, and only Yin Jiafu (age 39), a native of Zhengzhou, Henan, was apprehended. Inside the room, a hand grenade (made in China), fifteen photos, a suitcase, and letters were found in the desk drawer, as well as a set of blue cloth shirt and trousers. A piece of paper with the names Wang Shoushan and Wu Mai was found in the trouser pocket on the bed. They were taken to the police station for interrogation. Yin confessed that the place was a contact point for the Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group, managed by Wang Shoushan, with Wu Mai as the food officer. The organization was originally located in Room 33, Xinping Apartment, Gengyu Lane, Pubai Road, and moved to No. 45 Daode Lane on the 3rd of this month (i.e., the day of the arrest). Based on the confession, the police sent detectives back to Daode Lane to wait and arrest accomplices. At the same time, they sent detectives to search the home of lawyer Wu Mai at No. 8 Garden Villa, Huanlong Road. Wu and his family were not at home, and only the maid, Chen Zhoushi from Yangzhou, was present. A business card of Wang Shoushan was found in the dresser on the third floor, and two delivery books were found on the bamboo bookshelf in the downstairs study, including letters from the Self-Help Association for Resisting Foreign Aggression and Yun Huifang (who was arrested for throwing a bomb at Maochang Foreign Cloth Store at No. 347 Minguo Road on August 5th of the previous year and sentenced by the Special No. 2 Court to two months' imprisonment with a two-year reprieve). The detectives took them back to the police station. They also went to Xinping Apartment to question the tea room attendant, Wang Xuekuan (age 32, native of Zhenjiang). Wang confessed that a guest who called himself Wang Abao came on March 14th of this year and first opened Room 33. On May 8th, he switched to Room 23 and left the apartment on the 27th. During that time, he had opened other rooms, but the numbers were no longer remembered. However, Wang often came with many people, and Yin Jiafu had also been there and had seen him. Wang sometimes wore Chinese clothes and sometimes Western clothes. After investigation, the police found that they had opened Rooms 25, 26, 28, 23, and 33 of Xinping Apartment from January 17th to May 27th. The plainclothes detectives waiting at No. 45 Daode Lane arrested two Cantonese youths in Western suits at 1:25 PM the next day (the 4th). One claimed to be Kuang Wenyi, 22 years old, working at the Yong'an Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Lan Road, and the other claimed to be Kuang Beihai, 27 years old, working at the Taicang Electric Light Factory. The two were uncle and nephew and had come to find Wang Shoushan. The detectives took them to the police station and began to investigate whether the defendants were related to the bombing of Ri Xin Zeng and De Sheng Xiang, two foreign goods stores on French Avenue. Ri Xin Zeng was bombed four times, with two bombs failing to explode and two exploding. Both bombs at De Sheng Xiang exploded. Yesterday afternoon, the police sent Yin and others to the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Local Court. Judge Li Changnian interrogated them. Yin, who was bald and wore a black cotton shirt and trousers with a white undershirt and shoes without socks, stood in the defendant's dock with the other two. First, the police lawyers, Fei Xizhen and Yao Zhaodi, stated the case, alleging that the defendants participated in an association for the purpose of committing crimes, using explosives, and intentionally harming the lives and property of others. They threw bombs at stores in the concession, causing damage. The defendants were charged with disrupting order, endangering public safety, and destroying property under Articles 158, 161, 190, 200, 201, 381, and 382 of the Criminal Code. The police submitted photographs of the seized hand grenades and other exhibits. The judge asked the defendants about their age and origin. As it was almost noon, the judge adjourned the hearing until the afternoon. At 3:30 PM, Judge Li and clerk Wang Baoxun returned to the Criminal Division to continue the interrogation. The police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, appeared in court. Yin Jiafu confessed that he had been a soldier in the 19th Route Army. After the Shanghai War, he was transferred to Fujian. After being discharged, he went to Guangdong and came to Shanghai in January of this year, living in a thatched shed behind No. 1415 Yinghua Lane, Robert's Road. Wang Dongcai introduced him to the Blood Soul Eliminate Traitors Group and gave him 20 yuan per month. The group was managed by Wang Shoushan, and Wu Mai was the investigator. Wang Shoushan was from Anhui, about 35 years old. He had also been a battalion commander in the 19th Route Army, so he was also acquainted with him. The bombing was carried out after Wu investigated and reported the details. He was sent to wait near the store. At the appropriate time, Wang Dongcai would give him the bomb and order him to throw it. Wang Dongcai would report the results to Wang Shoushan. He threw bombs four times in the British and French concessions. The first time was in January at a certain foreign goods store on French Avenue (i.e., Ri Xin Zeng). The second and third times were in March at two foreign goods stores near the Xianshi Company on Fourth Avenue and Wuxi Road in the British Concession, both in alleys. The fourth time was in May at a foreign goods store in Zhengjia Wood Bridge (i.e., De Sheng Xiang). Of the four bombings, two exploded and two did not. He did not know the people who were identified by the detectives when they were arrested. On the day of his arrest, he was at home when Dongcai came and called him to clean the room at No. 45 Daode Lane. Wang escaped, and he was arrested. He did not know who had hidden the seized hand grenade there. He did not know where the two Wangs had fled to. He did not know Kuang and the others. Kuang Wenyi confessed that Wang Shoushan was his mother-in-law's adopted son and was introduced to him by his wife, but only for less than a month. Wang told him that he had just moved to No. 45 Daode Lane, so he went to visit him with his uncle that afternoon and was arrested. He knew nothing about the bombs. Kuang Beihai confessed that he had just come to Shanghai from Taicang three days ago and was living in the Qingnian Apartment on North Sichuan Road. He was arrested with his nephew Wenyi that day and claimed to know nothing about the bombs. As he did not speak Shanghainese, he could not answer the remaining questions but claimed to know nothing about the bombs. At this point, the plainclothes detectives reported the circumstances of the arrest of the defendants. The judge ordered the arguments to begin. After the police lawyer made the arguments, the court announced that the arguments were concluded and that the verdict would be announced on a scheduled date. The defendants were taken back into custody, and the court adjourned at 5:30 PM.

Guild Hall Refuses to Accept Coffin of Traitor 129

Hu Lifu Changes Name to Hu Junyuan

The traitor Hu Lifu was executed in Suzhou by strangulation. Hu was 53 years old and had four sons (one of whom was a lawyer). Upon hearing the news in Shanghai, his third son took 300 yuan in cash (the youngest son was still in school and did not go) and took the early morning express train to Suzhou. At the Sishi Street branch prison, he signed a statement to claim the body for coffining. He immediately spent 150 yuan in Suzhou to buy a coffin and clothes, and hired four porters to carry the coffin to Changmen. He paid to hire a small steamboat to transport the coffin to Shanghai that day. Yesterday morning, the boat arrived at Xinzha Bridge and asked a local bailiff named Ling to find a guild hall. Fearing that Hu was a traitor, the guild hall refused to allow the coffin to be stored there. He changed his name to Hu Junyuan and hired workers to carry the coffin into a temporary special room. The annual fee for storing the coffin was estimated at 8 yuan. He planned to choose another date to transport the coffin back to his ancestral home in Yongjia for burial.

Police Bust Electricity Theft Ring 130

More Than Sixty People Involved in Electricity Theft

Hundreds of Cases Committed

Lu Liankui, the Chinese Chief Detective of the Public Concession Police's General Inspection Department, and Chinese Detective Shao Jingfan recently cracked a large-scale electricity theft ring and arrested the criminals Cheng Zhangcai, Zhang Yulin, Liu Zhaoji, Zhao Xingkui, Huang Youliang, Ding Jintao, Wang Genfa, Yang Jingfu, Zhou Wenliang, Zhou Yiqing, Fan Chushan, and others. Most of them were employees and workers of the power company. More than sixty people were involved in the electricity theft. The police are investigating the details of the crime. Yesterday morning, the police sent the arrested Cheng Zhangcai and the other twelve to the First Special Court. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that although the case was a theft case, the actual situation was extremely serious. The number of people involved in the crime was large, and the number of cases committed was no less than several hundred. As far as the police knew, there were already more than two hundred cases. Therefore, the investigation would take some time. The matter was of great importance to the security and order of the concession, and the remaining accomplices were being pursued. Therefore, the trial could not proceed today, and it was requested that the trial be postponed for two weeks and a special court be opened to hear the case. The defendants, represented by lawyers Jiang Yiping, Shen Xingxia, Lin Yingqing, Du Jimei, and Lu Qi, requested bail, an earlier trial date, or exemption from sending them to Western Jail before the verdict was reached. Feng Shide, the presiding judge of the Criminal Court, ordered that the defendants be detained and postponed the trial to 2:00 PM on the 23rd of this month. The police were allowed to request the release of any defendants who were not related to the case at any time.

County Agricultural Education Center Trials Mint Planting 139

Increase Production: Resist Foreign Goods

The Shanghai County Zhuanqiao Farmers' Education Center has repeatedly received instructions from the County Government Education Bureau stating that mint is a major raw material for modern industry and medicine, with a high demand, but the domestic quantity is quite small, insufficient to meet demand. The import of foreign goods increases annually, causing a significant outflow of wealth, which is regrettable. China's soil is fertile, and if planting can be promoted, agricultural production can be increased. Planting mint is not subject to waterlogging, drought, or famine, and can supplement the shortage of beans, grains, and vegetables. Given the current state of agriculture in our county, planting should be vigorously promoted to enrich the people. Upon receiving the order, Director Zhang of the Center has begun planting in the open field, leading by example for the farmers. If the results are excellent in the future, it will be vigorously promoted.

Police Officer's Gun Discharges, Killing Elderly Clerk in Tragic Accident 144

On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at approximately 4:00 PM, Tian Chunyao, police officer No. 2350 of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau of Zhabei, was on duty in front of the Zhengchanghe Rice Store near the Xinzha Bridge on Datong Road. The officer was cleaning his handgun when, for unknown reasons, he inadvertently triggered the mechanism. A bullet fired from the gun, heading straight into the rice store. It struck Zhou Zhangzhi, a 30-year-old clerk from Tongzhou who worked at the store, hitting a vital area. Zhou immediately fell to the ground, bleeding profusely. Qiu Wen, the owner of the store, witnessed the incident and ordered someone to take Zhou to the Western Tibetan Road Epidemic Hospital, but the hospital refused to accept him. He was then transferred to Renji Hospital, where he died despite medical treatment. The hospital reported the incident to the Huishi Police Department, which dispatched investigators to investigate. The body was moved to the Feilun Road morgue for examination. The officer, realizing that he had caused an accident, knew there was no escape and was taken into custody by another officer at the Fourth District Bureau. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court reported the incident and appointed Prosecutor Guo Wei to visit the morgue to examine the body and conduct a public inquiry. According to Qiu Wen, 37 years old, a local and owner of the store, he was in the store having a haircut when he saw the officer cleaning the gun. He was only a few steps away and asked him if the gun was loaded. The officer replied that it was. Unexpectedly, at that moment, the bullet was discharged. Qiu also stated that the officer and the deceased did not know each other. Shen Kezhi, a police chief dispatched by the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, stated that the officer involved in the incident had been taken into custody at the bureau pending interrogation and transfer to the General Bureau. After receiving the evidence, Guo determined that Zhou Zhangzhi died from a gunshot wound. The body was released to Zhou Wen after he signed a guarantee for burial. As the crime occurred in the inland area, the suspect, officer No. 2350, should be handled by the inland court in accordance with the law.

Due to the brisk sales of Japanese goods in various Yangtze River ports, Japanese merchants have recently been rushing to load large quantities of Japanese goods in Shanghai, with some being transferred to various Yangtze River ports. The transport ship entered the port at noon today and immediately unloaded the military equipment at the Huishan and Osaka docks into the armory.
