Gleanings from Suzhou 196

— Yu Youqing

Zhou Shaofu Died Peacefully, Known Throughout the Country for His Good at Collecting Small Ornaments, Zhou Shaofu, who was known throughout the country, passed away peacefully the other day. Zhou was uninhibited throughout his life and not good at managing his household. He devoted all his energy to small ornaments and also loved his drink. He was amiable and approachable, especially regardless of class and age. Those who knew him felt like old friends at first sight. Small ornaments after this, it is feared that continuers will become the Guangling Extinction Sound.

▲ The Traitor Hu Lifu is Dead, the traitor Hu Lifu, was changed from life imprisonment to the death penalty and was hanged in the Third Prison the other day. Before his death, he still made arrogant remarks, saying, "It is right for me to die. If the traitors within the country can be wiped out from now on, the country will not perish. However, what will happen to those whose crimes are greater than mine?" People are about to die, and their words are good. This statement is indeed credible.

▲ Dong Xiujia's Wonderful Words and Deeds, Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department, Mr. Dong Xiujia came to Suzhou the other day to inspect the Jialu Road. Someone asked Mr. Dong whether he thought Suzhou's position as a hub for Beijing and Shanghai and the importance of its transportation warranted an expansion of construction, rather than a reduction in the size of the Construction Bureau, expressing his doubt. Could it be that he was trying to seek relief in the future? Mr. Dong said that the provincial treasury was extremely tight and that austerity measures were being implemented to seek remedies. All provincial committees advocate for abolition, and there is nothing that can be done. If I object, people will say that I am biased. But from a practical point of view, if you really want to do things, even the original Construction Bureau is not enough. If you don't do things, even the existing technician's office is excessive. When he came to Suzhou, he went to Room 10 of the Railway Hotel in Changmen. Upon arriving at the hotel, he paid the room rate in full and hosted a banquet for Qian Tianpeng and others. He is an honest official under party rule.

Whereabouts

A Trip to Fengming Mountain 197

— Daoyuan

Shangyu is a place where the Jin Prince Xie Lou hid and traveled, known for its scenic mountains and rivers, endowed with extraordinary energy, and producing talents. I had heard of its reputation but had not been able to visit. In the early summer of Gui Si, I organized the Shangyu Red Swastika Society and finally fulfilled my long-cherished wish. On the 28th, I made an appointment with my colleagues to visit Fengming Mountain. The mountain is more than ten miles south of the city. At first, I did not know how far it was, but as we went, it became further and further. The stone path wound around like the Yellow River's nine bends. The peaks were all tall and embraced the clouds. The sound of water was trickling by the roadside, and the scenery was secluded. When we reached the foot of the mountain, we looked up at the layers of stone steps, lush trees, and misty clouds. A high pavilion emerged, as if in mid-air, impossibly high. My fellow travelers all wanted to retreat, but I, at the age of sixty, still had great ambitions. I mustered my courage and went straight up to the top, and I did not feel tired, perhaps because of my seated meditation practice? After reaching the top of the mountain, we sat on the ground for a while and followed the path into a temple. The temple keeper, surnamed Du, named Xinchang, was over fifty years old, neither a Taoist nor a monk. He was old and sick and could not serve guests. The mountain produces tea, which has a very pure fragrance. The mountain dwellers cook it to serve the guests. Those who are thirsty find it like drinking jade nectar. Looking up at the temple, the main hall has three bays, surrounded by six bays of buildings on the left and right. The temple has a Dream God Hall. Every year during the Winter Solstice, men and women who want to divine good and bad fortune flock here, staying in the buildings on the left and right to pray for dreams. The dreams are often miraculously accurate. The temple is named Xiangu (Fairy Maiden), and it is said that in the Han Dynasty, a fairy maiden rode a luan to this place. After the fairy left, the villagers built a temple to worship her. To the left of the temple is a waterfall, hanging from the mountainside. Its sound is similar to the sound of pine waves, with dragons roaring and tigers howling. All worries should be washed away here. Beside the waterfall is a stone cave, also named after the fairy maiden, which is the place where the fairy rested. The cave is deep, remote, and quiet, with only enough space for one mat. It cannot accommodate people, and its entrance has been blocked by later generations. As I was gazing intently, suddenly a bird flew and chirped into the stone crevices. Its color was green, as big as a magpie with a long tail. Its sound was different from ordinary birds. Brother Huang Jiwu said it was a qingluan (green luan), but I did not believe it. When I returned, I read the Silk Records, which stated that this mountain had a fairy maiden riding a luan that sang like a phoenix. She rested in this building, and the mountain was named after it. After the fairy left, the luan stayed behind, and some people still saw it. The qingluan I saw was smaller in size, perhaps a descendant of the fairy luan? We have lived in Shanghai for a long time, with its bustling and noisy environment. Our ambitions and thoughts are dim and unclear. Being here, worldly thoughts are dispelled, and the mind and spirit are refreshed. I think of the decline of the world, the frequent disasters in recent years, and the people living as if in a nightmare. We eagerly await the return of the phoenix singing in seclusion, but it is not possible. Now that the qingluan has appeared, is it a harbinger of the arrival of the phoenix bird? Therefore, I am happy to record this.

Returning from Songjiang 198

— Chuan Yizhi

Songjiang has two famous products: one is the yellow peach, as big as a goose egg, with flesh that is fresh, sweet, and delicious, superior to ordinary peaches; the other is the four-gill perch. It is said that they are both produced in the same harbor, with the perches at both ends of the harbor having three gills, and only those caught in the central harbor having four gills. Because of its unique advantage, it can survive for ten days out of water without dying. In the past, people used to present it to the imperial court as tribute. Su Shi's "Later Ode to the Red Cliff" mentioned "a huge mouth and fine scales, resembling the perch of Songjiang," which probably refers to this.

My friend Mr. Zhou established a New Agricultural Beekeeping Farm in western Zhejiang. This spring, he moved his hives there and invited me to visit him in Songjiang. Last Sunday morning, I took the train there. After getting off at Mingxing Bridge, I asked for the location of the beekeeping farm. The local farmers and women led me with enthusiasm and were not tired of talking. This is the innate nature of human mutual assistance, but it is no longer possible to find it in Shanghai. There are three beekeeping farms east of the city, but they are all temporary. Once the flowering season is over, they have to move again. The New Agricultural Beekeeping Farm established by my friend is one of them. The farm has been in operation for three years, with an investment of over four thousand yuan. It currently has about one hundred and forty hives, each with five to ten frames of honeycomb foundation. Mr. Zhou showed me the honeycomb foundation, and all the cells filled with ripened honey were sealed. The bees were buzzing and flying around, constantly going in and out. I joked to Mr. Zhou: "Who are these busy little guys working for?" He said: "They are preparing for the winter food supply, and also for their own survival. However, with human intelligence, we can use them to extract honey for profit. But in spring, there are chrysanthemums and purple vetches, in summer, there are tallow trees and sesame, and in autumn, there is buckwheat and winter loquat. By moving the hives to different locations, we never let them starve to death, which is better than simply exploiting them." I listened and remained silent.

The farm is about one kilometer away from the east gate, with fields stretching in all directions and clouds and water reflecting each other. The village women wrap their heads and go barefoot, either working in the fields or carrying firewood on the road. Who says that Chinese women are all parasites? From the east gate to the west gate, the street is about ten miles long, with shops lined up side by side, offering a unique flavor. However, the cloth shops all display Indian silk and foreign yarn cloth, which further proves that foreign goods are invading our country's market like water flowing downhill, and there is no place they do not reach. I cannot help but feel a sense of melancholy!

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Pass Quietly 199

The gold market was quite stable yesterday. There was a brief rise in the middle, but the result was flat. In the morning, due to the overseas silver market squeeze on the 4th and 6th, the British pound rose and the U.S. dollar fell. Exchange rates continued to show a slight rise. The gold exchange's forward silver prices and stocks both fell before rising again. The U.S. cotton squeeze rebounded by several points, which was disappointing. The raw cotton market opened flat. Bing Xingfen sold actively in the market, and Yuan Maoyong also sold on his behalf, reaching a price of about 39 yuan. The exchange market opened without strengthening. Zhifeng, Yongheng, and Yu all advanced. The Dalian gang smoothly purchased according to the listed price, and the opening was flat. After entering the market, the domestic market was tighter. HSBC's listed British and U.S. rates both shrank by 1.25. People's minds were more stable. In addition, the Guangdong gang Hengxing vigorously purchased, and simultaneously deducted U.S. dollars. The situation rose accordingly. The later market was initially flat. Finally, Bombay rose slightly, but the bank's appetite was weak and fell. The situation was mediocre throughout the day. Reports stated that the Ministry of Finance had borrowed 50 million yuan and used four-fifths of it to purchase U.S. cotton. However, the power was not great, and the price increase was not expected to be significant, so it had no major impact. Bullish Sentiment Emerges in Securities Market 204

A Small Rebound Suddenly Arises in the Bond Market 205

▲Cumbersome Accounting Procedures, Separate Trading Sessions Morning and Afternoon▲

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange saw a sudden rebound in public bonds, with strong recovery momentum. Due to extremely cumbersome accounting procedures throughout the day, only one trading session was held in the morning and one in the afternoon. As bullish sentiment emerged from various groups, market prices experienced significant fluctuations. However, short covering and bargain hunting were also quite active. The morning session opened late, starting at 11:00 AM. Initially, market prices were quite firm. 1918 Customs bonds rose 3 jiao, and Reorganization bonds rose 4 to 5 jiao. This month's demobilization bonds rose from an opening price of 64 yuan and 8 jiao, gradually increasing to a peak of 65 yuan and 7 jiao. At this point, major players suddenly sold off large quantities, and market prices fell from high to low, closing at 64 yuan and 7 jiao. The rapid changes caused extreme anxiety. 1919 Customs bonds opened at 48 yuan and 2 jiao, gradually falling to 47 yuan and 2 jiao. The significant fluctuations and the downward trend were due to strong buying interest, but the competition between bulls and bears ultimately led to a slight decline due to oversupply. Subsequently, various other bonds followed this pattern, decreasing by around 1 yuan each. Trading was extremely active. In the afternoon session, Reorganization bonds opened sharply lower by 2 yuan and 7 jiao, with a minimum price of 61 yuan and 7 jiao. The difference between the highest and lowest prices was a significant 4 yuan. Such large fluctuations and market volatility have been rare recently, but compared to the previous day, the price only fell by 9 jiao. The reasons for this include the emergence of bullish sentiment and the use of arbitrage by bulls due to significant differences between near-term and long-term contracts. Therefore, the long-term contracts only decreased by a small amount of 1 yuan, which was insufficient. However, 1920s treasury bonds remained firm and even slightly increased by 1 to 2 jiao, up to 5 to 6 jiao. As a result, they fell by 8 jiao to 1 yuan and 3 jiao compared to the previous day. This stable rebound often occurs after significant increases and decreases, which is a natural human reaction and often unavoidable. The total trading volume was 18,699,000 yuan, including 14,000 yuan in spot trading. Futures trading was dominated by salt taxes, accounting for 5,795,000 yuan, followed by 1919 Customs bonds at 2,985,000 yuan, 1920s Gan Customs bonds at 3,730,000 yuan, and other bonds ranging from 6,000,000 to 75,000 yuan.

A telegram from Singapore reported that there are no spot goods in the near future, and a certain tin merchant in Hong Kong is hoarding large quantities. Due to this extreme shortage of supply, market sentiment in Shanghai is very fearful. Standard tin continued to rise sharply, with small mine tin opening at 170 yuan, a further increase of 10 yuan. Dutch tin opened at 188 yuan, an increase of 8 yuan. Jianghua Hengdi and other tins also increased by 4 to 5 yuan. The strong purchasing interest from Sichuan and Shaoxing merchants and local factories is driving up prices, and there is a high probability that the market will continue to improve.

Commentary

Magic Tricks 219

"Everyone can perform magic tricks, but each has their own unique skills." These lines are the opening remarks of artists on stage. Magic tricks are originally a set of performances. Whether you are Eastern, Western, or Chinese, no matter how well you perform or how unpredictable you are, you cannot escape some skills in your technique. If you do well, everyone applauds and praises you. If you do poorly, the audience will boo, and naturally, the artist will lose face. In reality, since it is called a magic trick, it is mostly fake, nothing more than a deceptive performance.

Therefore, the jargon of magicians says, "Magic has no truth. Reveal it on the spot." In reality, where would a magician be willing to reveal it? If they were to reveal it, it would be worthless. Therefore, what can be revealed are only some superficial things, and the content will never be revealed. However, since it is a magic trick, anyone can know that what they are performing is not real. Even if it is not revealed on the spot, believing it to be real is probably extremely rare, and there are probably no such fools. However, because they perform skillfully, they earn the surprise and speculation of the general audience, who say it is performed this way or that way. The benevolent see benevolence, and the wise see wisdom, leaving people in a fog, ultimately unsure of the true meaning.

However, there is one point that artists must understand. No matter how well you perform, everyone knows it is fake, knows it is a sleight of hand, knows it is a misdirection, knows it is a show of pretense. Everyone recognizes this point. However, even though everyone recognizes it, the artist still has to perform. Fortunately, the audience has already bought tickets and entered the venue, sitting under this stage, unafraid that you won't watch. If you watch, naturally you will pay money. If you don't watch, you will still pay money. You can only watch, sit under the stage dozing off, stretching your lazy face, and shouting that you're bored, which has nothing to do with us.

This is originally a customary skill of artists.

Children and Social Education 221

— Ping

I remember when I was five or six years old, although I had entered elementary school, it was an incomplete school. Generally, children in this place did not make any new discoveries. Every child followed the "gentle and refined" model of the teacher. After school, groups of three or five would choose a secluded and dark doorway to gather and begin telling stories. Stories like Sun Wukong somersaulting 108,000 miles but unable to escape the Buddha's palm; Zhang Fei riding a yellow mule, standing at the head of Changban Bridge, shouting and frightening Cao Cao's 800,000 troops into running away in terror; and the story of Lu Dongbin and the Eight Immortals crossing the sea—this type of unfounded, baseless tales were told every day until they were thoroughly memorized. Not only did the audience listen as usual, but the teller still felt more and more interested. At the time, it seemed like the dozen or so children in our village were not intelligent at all. If I heard a new story elsewhere, I would immediately return, gather everyone, and tell it tirelessly for several days. In addition, there were games like running factory walls, planting melons and beans, killing sheep, and jumping gates, all unsuitable for children's personalities.

After the Revolutionary Army established itself in the Yangtze River basin, the actions of children changed: lining up, blowing horns, and everyone carving a knife or sword. After school, they began practicing combat, abandoning the previous habit of not distinguishing between streets and alleys, drawing boundaries, killing each other, and hating each other. It reached the point where a child dared not freely move outside the boundaries. Even the stories they liked to listen to were about overthrowing warlords and overthrowing imperialism.

In recent years, even more progress has been made. Scattered children have formed teams, with flags, wooden guns, captains, commanders, and guards carrying cigarette boxes made into pistols to protect the commander, as well as detectives, etc. They call themselves the Revolutionary Army and call the opposing children midgets and devils. When they meet, they shout kill. Overthrow, charge, resolve, and report are all spoken fluently. They also give speeches and slogans. They commonly use stones instead of bullets to practice combat. Both sides agree on a time, find an open space as a battlefield, and at the sound of a bugle, they all start, and stones rain down. When someone is bleeding, everyone thinks they have achieved their goal, applauds loudly, and triumphantly returns. The children who are hit also find it interesting, wrap the wound with a handkerchief, and discuss the method of sharing the spoils with their companions, never shrinking back. They have to hide it from their families. Children's changes, in this evolutionary process, are constantly influenced by social suggestions. Children consider the social state's evolution to be novel and interesting, and its influence is imitated everywhere. In summary, we should dare to pay attention to the following points:

1. From literary to martial.

2. From scattered to organized.

3. From stillness to movement.

4. From rigid to lively, especially in terms of thought, progress is really fast. The knowledge of children who are now seven or eight years old exceeds that of children who were thirteen or fourteen years old one or two decades ago. We must know that social progress is fast, and children's thinking progresses quickly. All of children's actions are a microcosm of the general state of society. If we want to improve the nation, then children's education is the first task.

Save the Youth 222

— Peng Nian

Everyone says that youth are the future masters of the nation and the future builders of society. The transformation of a new nation, the construction of a new society, and everything else, all rely on the strength of youth to advance and develop. Therefore, it is said that the strength of youth can produce national wealth, and the strength of youth can expand social development. To make the country strong and society good, it is necessary to cultivate, value, and care for youth first. Although this is what is said, there are many people who do not do this, perhaps intentionally, but instead go to harm them. What is the reason for this? Look: "The newspaper reports that a certain youth committed suicide out of concern for the country, a certain youth committed suicide due to heartbreak, and a certain youth committed suicide due to being out of school..." These are facts that can be seen in the newspapers every day, and I don't need to elaborate. However, regarding those who commit suicide,

Page 18

Whether it is due to a flawed social system or out of free will, this is a question worthy of in-depth study. If the suicide is out of free will, then why doesn't the suicide victim say in their suicide note, "I willingly die"? Instead, they write, "Unable to achieve XX, I committed suicide." From this, it seems that most people who commit suicide are not willing to do so.

Is there any benefit to the country or society from having many suicides? I think not necessarily. Didn't I say earlier? "Youth are the future masters of the nation and the future builders of society." Since youth are capable of being the future masters of the nation and the builders of society, they naturally have the ability to do so and the shoulders to bear this great responsibility. Otherwise, would people call them that? If that's the case, then harming one youth is like harming a portion of the nation's vitality, and losing one youth is like losing a portion of society's strength. Alas! If the country does not cultivate them,

If society does not value them, it seems they have no reason to cherish themselves either.

You reap what you sow. In short, this is the result of a flawed social system. For example, "If a sailing ship at sea loses its rudder, can that ship remain steady? It will inevitably drift with the waves and will never sail on a straight course." Whose responsibility is this? This is naturally the fault of the helmsman. Isn't the relationship between society and youth just like this? Therefore, to reduce youth suicide, we must first reform the social system. Otherwise, all youth will follow the tide of suicide and drift away with the waves.

Various Types of Shanghai Beggars 223

— Chang

(1) Chasing "Piglets"

As long as you have sharp eyes, follow those modern couples holding hands and say a few words: "Young master and young mistress! May you be happy and prosperous!" If they are pleased, with her giggle, he will naturally scatter a handful of copper coins from his suit pocket, or perhaps a dime.

(2) Greeting Cars

This is a top-notch business that earns money without effort. As long as you occupy the territory of several large companies, large hotels, dance halls, and Western restaurants, when a shiny black-plated car stops, you quickly stretch out your arms and open the car door, shouting, "Young master! Miss, have a good trip!" The price is at least twenty cents.

(3) Lodging Complaints

To do this business, you shouldn't dress too raggedly, to show that you are a temporary down-on-your-luck from another hometown. Moreover, you must be able to write well with chalk and understand some foreign languages. It is very suitable for someone like me, a former elementary school teacher, to switch to this. However, the income is far less than greeting cars.

(4) Guarding Temple Gates

Guarding the temple gate was previously called "relying on the stone lion." Its target customers are exactly the opposite of chasing "piglets." Muttering "Namo" to the old-fashioned ladies of the eighteenth century, and saying a few words like "Accumulate blessings and longevity," you are guaranteed to be satisfied.

(5) Collecting Bridge Tolls

Those who collect bridge tolls are mostly newcomers who have just started out. However, even helping to pull rickshaws up the bridge, I heard that they can earn a thousand or eight hundred [copper coins] a day. (6) Eating Leftovers

This belongs to the enjoyment aspect, and the insider term is "摸蟹 [mō xiè, groping for crabs]". After lunch and dinner at various shops and households every day, the leftovers from the food vendors are usually a treat for the 三黨 [sān dǎng, three parties - beggars]. Although these dishes are mostly leftovers, with fresh fish, fatty meat, and seasonal vegetables and fruits, they can greatly satisfy the appetite.

Since being a beggar in Shanghai has such great income and such enjoyment, it is no wonder that so many young masters are desperately trying to crawl into their nests.

Shop Assistant Communications

Whose Son? 225

Editor:

I am a poor boy. My parents died when I was young, and I can't remember whose son I am. A Taoist priest named Feng raised me until I was eight years old. Later, his wife also died, and there was no one to raise me, so I lived in the open wilderness. Finally, a clerk from the Township Office of this town, surnamed Yu, took me to his home. He and his wife were both over forty years old and very kind. Since they had no children, they treated me as their son. But the clan objected, and I could not be named as a descendant of the Yu family, but only as an adopted son. Since I didn't remember my biological father, I took the surname of the Taoist priest Feng, and was named Feng. Unexpectedly, this spring, my adoptive father, surnamed Yu, died. His death was extremely difficult, and even the funeral was done hastily with the help of the clan. Although my adoptive mother is very distressed, she cannot bear to drive me away. Now the two of us are living a hard life. However, my adoptive father owed a lot of debts during his lifetime. Although he has two brothers, they are unrelated, and the creditors still come every day to demand payment. My adoptive mother cries all day long, and has nothing in her hands. The clan members can chip in a few coins to buy rice, but it is impossible to take out money to pay off my dead adoptive father's debts. I am only thirteen years old now, and I have no ability to earn money. If my adoptive mother is forced to death by the creditors, my little life will also be gone. I don't want to be a fourth son again, so I might as well throw myself into the river and die. Good-hearted sirs, what methods are there to save the lives of my mother and son! The poor child Feng Guxiang kowtows.

Editor's note: In this era of economic decline, it is very common for a person to owe some debts. Fortunately, this common phenomenon has been pitied by legislators. Now the laws of any country, including China, treat debtors in this way: unless they intentionally conceal their property with the intention of being lazy, then they will be punished; if they really cannot pay, then there is no guilt. Acts like cutting off flesh to pay debts are now prohibited. "Not afraid of the fierce, only afraid of the poor" has almost been tacitly approved by the law. If this is the case for one's own debts, then the debts owed by a spouse during their lifetime, and the debts owed by the person being inherited during their lifetime, can be ignored even more. You mother and son are now so poor. In theory, others should be afraid of you. What are you afraid of others for? Now, the Yu clan is willing to chip in a few coins for you to buy rice, which is very fortunate. You should now advise your adoptive mother not to take everything to heart; just eat yellow rice and dried radish, and try to add to your meals. You should invigorate your ambition, wait for an opportunity, know the sweetness and bitterness, to find a way out in the future. Finally, we hope that those who read this letter will provide assistance within their means.

At this time, Fifth Concubine felt very awkward, unable to be unrestrained, and Manager Gu understood that Fifth Concubine was no longer the former Miss Liu.

"So, you're coming from your residence now?" Mr. Gu said again.

"Ah! That's great, that's great."

As he spoke, Mr. Gu shook her hand again and went out. Fifth Concubine sat in the car and went home. Naturally, she couldn't help but recall the intimate scenes of the past, but a hug from Young Master Zhang dismissed them.

24. Crime and Punishment

Minister Su had returned from Beijing four or five days ago. But these few days he had been staying at the Second Concubine's place. He came to this place for one night the day before yesterday and was very happy, but today it was very different. He walked in with a murderous aura, as if he wanted to eat people. Fifth Concubine naturally immediately greeted him and led him into the bedroom, but he became even more angry, slapped the table and pointed at He Xiang and scolded:

"Quick! You bunch of dogs! Go and call that kid Zhang out here."

"You kid! What are you? How dare you be so bold?! Get out! Get out!... Get out of here now!"

"What's this all about? Why are you so angry?" Fifth Concubine couldn't help but speak at this time.

"What's the matter? You still ask me what's the matter? How dare you shameless people ask me? Gu Shoujie will"

"He told me everything about you, is there anything wrong? You've lost all the hundreds of thousands of deposits in the Taiwan Bank."

"Hmph! What a great thing you've done!"

"There's nothing to say now, tell Zhang Wenbin to leave here immediately, leave immediately, hurry!"

At this time, Fifth Concubine was extremely angry. Seeing Zhang Wenbin retreating without daring to say a word, she became even more angry, almost shedding tears. She glared at the old man Su, smiled proudly, as if she was full of confidence, and said calmly:

"Okay, old man, you're bullying me now. You're embarrassing me like this, you know who he is."

"Okay, you're now in breach of contract. Do you remember what you promised me before?"

However, Minister Su couldn't show weakness at this time. He took advantage of a burst of anger and rushed out the door.

Movie Special

Wednesday, June 7, 1933 The Shun Pao Screen Section

A Glimpse of Hollywood Studios 227

— Heng

Rationalized Divisional Organization

Is the Biggest Reason for Development

It is truly amazing that movies have made such great progress in such a short period of time. It wasn't long ago that large, rationalized organizations and the expansion of various equipment replaced the outdoor production studios under the sun and the clumsy glass sheds of the past. Now, major Hollywood film companies have built their own small cities.

Within the walls of each company, it is divided into several zones, with residential areas, industrial areas, commercial areas, etc., built under the intersection of short streets and flat roads for several miles. The equipment inside includes hospitals and schools, forcing children of school age to read for several hours a day, agile fire brigade stations, teahouses, and restaurants. In addition to this, there are vast production studios. There are several photography studios themselves, towering libraries, production departments, makeup departments, screenwriting departments, publicity departments, and other executive departments. Of course, the accounting department is also very important among them, and the police are naturally the most important equipment inside. Their duties are to maintain the order of road administration, pay attention to crowded days, crowd congestion, and guard and protect the transportation of money, especially when transferring to distant places. In short, their task is to protect the welfare of the entire film city.

The rationalized divisional organization can be said to be the biggest reason for the great progress in film technology. The results of research and experimentation have given amazing advances to lighting, cameras, sets, and sound, and have perfected various technologies.

A film must go through many stages, that is, the selection of stories, the allocation of actors, the setting of scenes, shooting, editing, and the technical cooperation of sound, to create a perfect "work of art." But there is a crisis here, that is, overemphasis on technology. "Clumsy technology can damage the film, but good technology has never produced bad films." (?) This is naturally the view of American Well-Made Plays, which only focuses on skill and ignores consciousness. Because it is not within the topic, I will not describe it further.

Movie Reviews

Review of "Stranger in Town" 228

— Ling He

Stranger in Town

In the current situation where the world's finances are in extreme chaos and the economy is collapsing, the collapse of banks and the unsmooth turnover of stores have become a common phenomenon in various countries around the world. The United States is of course no exception, and it is the most obvious, especially when Roosevelt took office as president. Of course, this turbulent upsurge is by no means an accidental phenomenon, but the existing economic organization is approaching the final inevitable stage of collapse.

Then, the small shops in this turmoil will naturally suffer great sacrifices and are the inevitable result that cannot be avoided. Therefore, it is indeed a very good choice for the author of "Stranger in Town" to use this as the theme, and at the same time, this very special situation will inevitably be reflected in the artistic works.

But how does the author of "Stranger in Town" understand this fresh theme? Indeed, many small shops will implement price reductions or other deformed auctions at this time in order to recover costs, and large capital entrepreneurs will reduce prices and try their best to sell due to the surplus of industrial products, and even direct sales, penetrating into every village. In this way, the market is more chaotic, and the competition in business is more acute. Of course, small capitalists will not be able to support it for a long time, not to mention that all goods need to be wholesale in cash, and banks have successively collapsed, making it impossible to turn around, and in the end, they can only close down and even go bankrupt.

But there is also an unavoidable phenomenon in the middle, that is, due to the reduction of prices, agricultural products are sold cheaply, resulting in rural bankruptcy and a reduction in purchasing power. Naturally, this is a big contradiction. Even if commodities are reduced in price, will they finally not teach customers to compete for purchases? However, the author of "Stranger in Town" ignored these, and he thought that as long as the price was reduced, the rural customers would flock to it. At the same time, when old man Kleeshill's grocery store was in trouble, it was said that the goods were not enough, and finally a large number of goods were obtained on credit due to the relationship of the granddaughter-in-law. And can this revive it? Naturally impossible.

As for such a theme, although the consciousness is inevitably blurred, it is very good to perform it in the form of comedy. At the same time, the interweaving of love, although not very necessary, is not forced. However, the prologue fifty years ago at the beginning is a superfluous scene. Some jokes are repetitive and exaggerated, and at the same time, a scene of love talk also feels that it somewhat damages the mood of the whole play. There is also the last truck running rampant, which is also a boring old trick. In short, this is not a very successful work for the director.

However, the performance of the protagonist is very commendable. Being able to exaggerate in a burlesque without going too far, and being so natural and reasonable, is really rare. The supporting actors are also very appropriate.

I think this is a very interesting work.

The "Maternal Light" directed by Bu Wancang of Lianhua No. 1 Factory is the most noticed film by social figures and the entire film industry. The sound part of this film is particularly noteworthy.

There are three songs in this film, and "Spring Love Song" is one of them.

Everyone is willing to know the lyrics of the song, so let us introduce it first. Although there are only a few words in this song, the song is short but the meaning is profound.

Spring Love Song

Flowers are swaying with the green waves,

Birds are singing on the flower branches! Waves are reflecting the beautiful setting sun, people are whispering on the magnolia boat.

Your eyes shot into my heart, your caress healed my pain! The most precious thing in the world is love: Ah! Love is supreme. We don't want to be immortals, we only want to be mandarin ducks! Don't want to be immortals, only want to be mandarin ducks!

This gentle and tender "Spring Love Song" is sung by the beautiful little bird - Chen Yanyan.

Huang Yunzhen Sends Dragon Boat Festival Rice Dumplings 231

Huang Yunzhen, who often plays the role of madam in Lianhua No. 2 Factory, is good at cooking and often entertains colleagues at home. Those who taste it always sigh, "It is enough to stop eating." Han Lagen Practices New Techniques 232

Han Lagen is naturally blessed with a crying face, and can make funny performances and movements in films, so he can win the favor of the audience. His special technical performances include moving his scalp, moving his ears, and tilting his eyeballs to the left and right, separating, matching, and rotating them extremely freely. This kind of performance was seen in the "Morning of the Metropolis" directed by Cai Chusheng of Lianhua. Recently, Han has been practicing a technique that allows him to move his eyelashes automatically without moving his eyelids. This technique has been practiced in front of the mirror every morning for two months, but he has not yet succeeded in making his eyelashes move automatically without moving his eyelids, although the eyelashes did move automatically once in the middle, but it was blown by the wind.

Ruan Lingyu and Xiao Yu Hold Vegetarian Meals Together 233

Recently, Ruan Lingyu doesn't know what kind of vegetarian diet she is eating, and she is very pious about it. She has been filming "Small Toys" at the Second Factory for days, from morning till night. Her lunch and dinner meals are delivered from home. Even her daughter Xiao Yu does not touch any meat. One day, when the staff in the factory were having a snack, Li Lili took a piece of bread smeared with White Pagoda oil and gave it to Xiao Yu. Xiao Yu was about to accept it when Ruan Lingyu caught a glimpse of it and called out, "N囡 [nānnǚ, child]: This is meat!" So Xiao Yu retracted her hand and dared not accept it.

Sun Yu's Son Refuses to Go to the Folk 234

Director Sun's eldest son Tommy is fat and cute. Yesterday, when filming the rural scenery of Sister-in-law Ye for "Small Toys", there were more than a dozen village children doing various games in the village. Mr. Sun brought his son with him in the morning, intending to have his son join the village children in the performance, but unexpectedly, when he was dressing him up in the makeup room, he firmly refused to take off his shoes, change into ragged clothes, and dress up as a village child. Soft words and hard words were not heard, and if forced, he cried loudly. Sun scolded him angrily. Tommy said, "You hit me, I'll go back and tell my mother, let my mother hit you!" At that time, Lu Yexing joked to Sun Yu on the side, "You specialize in making plays that describe the folk, but your son refuses to go to the folk."

Novel, Film, Female Radiance: Maedchen in Uniform (2) 235

— By Xin Fu

Produced by German Film Company, Starring an Entire Cast of Female Actors

"Ms. Pei Bo! What kind of person is she? Why is that girl so infatuated with her?" She thought to herself, but she was unwilling to ask the smug clerk, so she exited the "dressing room," holding onto the staircase railing, walking down step by step languidly. Coincidentally, Ms. Pei Bo was walking up towards her, face to face. When Pei Bo saw Manilla's pitiful appearance, even though it was their first meeting, she couldn't help but feel a sense of affection. When Manilla reached her, she reached out and stroked her braids, examining her face for a while, and then asked, "What's your name? Are you new here?" Manilla answered her truthfully, and then they each went their separate ways.

In her disappointment, Manilla suddenly encountered this gentle and elegant teacher, and her almost dead heart seemed to gradually revive. Pei Bo walked upstairs, and she stood there alone, looking at her receding figure. Suddenly, a classmate patted her on the shoulder and gently asked her, "Do you know this teacher? She is the kindest of all the teachers, the Ms. Pei Bo that all the students in the school admire!" Manilla now understood. The heart and letters on the uniform were indeed so. Thus, her sorrow seemed to vanish into thin air, and a smile gradually reappeared on her face.

In the dormitory, many lovely little girls were sitting and standing, some doing needlework, some chatting and laughing. Among them was a little girl named Alice, who had many photos of men pasted behind her closet. Wasn't this a fresh and interesting piece of news? So everyone gathered around her and teased her. Over there, another female student was holding a letter from home, shouting, "My mother said she killed a pig, why doesn't she send me ham to eat!" This sentence elicited another burst of laughter. At this moment, they suddenly heard leather shoes outside. A detective standing by the door hurriedly gave her classmates a meaningful look. Everyone knew that the teacher was coming, and they immediately fell silent.

Now, let's talk about the kitchen. Groups of female cooks were talking animatedly. A maid ran in very hurriedly and said, "The students are clamoring that they are hungry, hurry up!" A cook put down the basin she was holding and turned around to say, "Hungry?" They are all the children of soldiers, and they will have to be the mothers of soldiers in the future; moreover, we Prussians are full of patience. Can't they even bear a hungry stomach?" Another said, "Half a pound of cream is to be distributed to fifty girls. It is very strange that so many girls have never complained. I will definitely give my share to them." (To be continued)
